           <h3 name="99fc" id="99fc" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--figure">Pre-Project Setup</h3>
           <p name="3dc8" id="3dc8" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Here’s what you’ll need:</p>
           <ul class="postList">
            <li name="58eb" id="58eb" class="graf graf--li graf-after--p"><a href="https://openweathermap.org/api" data-href="https://openweathermap.org/api" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><strong class="markup--strong markup--li-strong">OpenWeatherMap.org</strong></a> account. It’s a quick 20 second signup?—?I walk through all the setup details <a href="https://codeburst.io/build-a-simple-weather-app-with-node-js-in-just-16-lines-of-code-32261690901d" data-href="https://codeburst.io/build-a-simple-weather-app-with-node-js-in-just-16-lines-of-code-32261690901d" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" target="_blank">here</a>.</li>
            <li name="88fb" id="88fb" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li"><strong class="markup--strong markup--li-strong">Node.js: </strong>Visit the official <a href="https://nodejs.org/en/" data-href="https://nodejs.org/en/" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Node.js website</a> to download and install Node if you haven’t already. Looking for a more in-depth tutorial on Node? Check out my <a href="https://codeburst.io/three-awesome-courses-for-learning-node-js-d7f761437101" data-href="https://codeburst.io/three-awesome-courses-for-learning-node-js-d7f761437101" class="markup--anchor markup--li-anchor" target="_blank">Top Three Node.js courses</a>.</li>
           </ul>
           <h3 name="664c" id="664c" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--li">Project Setup</h3>
           <blockquote name="7785" id="7785" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--h3">
            Before we begin, all the code for this project can be found in the 
            <a href="https://github.com/bmorelli25/simple-nodejs-weather-app" data-href="https://github.com/bmorelli25/simple-nodejs-weather-app" class="markup--anchor markup--blockquote-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">GitHub Repo</a>
           </blockquote>
           <ol class="postList">
            <li name="b311" id="b311" class="graf graf--li graf-after--blockquote">Create an empty directory named <code class="markup--code markup--li-code">weather-app</code>.</li>
            <li name="92ad" id="92ad" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li">Open up your console, navigate to our new directory and run <code class="markup--code markup--li-code">npm init</code>.</li>
            <li name="611a" id="611a" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li">Fill out the required information to initialize our project.</li>
            <li name="9825" id="9825" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li">Within our <code class="markup--code markup--li-code">weather-app</code> directory, create a file named <code class="markup--code markup--li-code">server.js</code>?—?this file will house the code for our application.</li>
           </ol>
           <p name="c7ae" id="c7ae" class="graf graf--p graf-after--li">Now that we have all the puzzle pieces, we can start building!</p>
           <h3 name="c144" id="c144" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Creating our Server (with Express&nbsp;JS)</h3>
           <p name="3863" id="3863" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">First thing we need to do is get our server up and running. We’re going to use <a href="https://expressjs.com/" data-href="https://expressjs.com/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Express </a>to accomplish this. Express is a minimalist web framework for <a href="https://codeburst.io/three-awesome-courses-for-learning-node-js-d7f761437101" data-href="https://codeburst.io/three-awesome-courses-for-learning-node-js-d7f761437101" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" target="_blank">Node.js</a>?—?Express makes it very easy to create and run a web server with Node.</p>
           <p name="efae" id="efae" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">To use express, install it in the console:</p>
           <pre name="d69f" id="d69f" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">npm install --save express</pre>
           <p name="fab5" id="fab5" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Once installed, we’re going to copy the boilerplate Express starter app from the <a href="https://expressjs.com/en/starter/hello-world.html" data-href="https://expressjs.com/en/starter/hello-world.html" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Express documentation</a>:</p>
           <pre name="a7c6" id="a7c6" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">const express = require('express')<br>const app = express()<br><br>app.get('/', function (req, res) {<br>  res.send('Hello World!')<br>})<br><br>app.listen(3000, function () {<br>  console.log('Example app listening on port 3000!')<br>})</code></pre>
           <p name="f9cb" id="f9cb" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Above is an example of the simplest application that we can create with Express. First we require the express package that was just installed. Then, we create an instance named <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">app</code> by invoking Express.</p>
           <p name="e2c4" id="e2c4" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">The <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">app.get('/'...</code> means we are specifically focusing on the root URL (<code class="markup--code markup--p-code">/</code>). If we visit the root URL, Express will respond with “Hello World!”.</p>
           <p name="6e67" id="6e67" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">The <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">app.listen(...</code> shows we are creating a server that is listening on port 3000 for connections.</p>
           <p name="390c" id="390c" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">We can test our server by running:</p>
           <pre name="6118" id="6118" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--pre-strong">node server.js</strong></pre>
           <pre name="0349" id="0349" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// <code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">Example app listening on port 3000!</code></pre>
           <p name="9c2a" id="9c2a" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Now open your browser and visit: <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">localhost:3000</code> and you should see Hello World!</p>
           <figure name="1639" id="1639" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 235px; max-height: 140px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 59.599999999999994%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*1jyKrmxYIiSrZphEgjgBQw.png" data-width="235" data-height="140">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*1jyKrmxYIiSrZphEgjgBQw.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <img class="progressiveMedia-image js-progressiveMedia-image" data-src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*1jyKrmxYIiSrZphEgjgBQw.png">
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <img class="progressiveMedia-noscript js-progressiveMedia-inner" src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/max/1600/1*1jyKrmxYIiSrZphEgjgBQw.png">
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="e400" id="e400" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Awesome! You’ve just created a server with <a href="https://codeburst.io/three-awesome-courses-for-learning-node-js-d7f761437101" data-href="https://codeburst.io/three-awesome-courses-for-learning-node-js-d7f761437101" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" target="_blank">Node.js</a> and Express!</p>
           <h3 name="c8af" id="c8af" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Setting up the index&nbsp;view</h3>
           <p name="95c2" id="95c2" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Instead of responding with text when someone visits our root route, we’d like to respond with an HTML file. For this, we’ll be using EJS (<a href="http://www.embeddedjs.com/" data-href="http://www.embeddedjs.com/" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Embedded JavaScript</a>). EJS is a <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">templating language.</em></p>
           <p name="69fe" id="69fe" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">In order to use EJS in Express, we need to set up our template engine:</p>
           <blockquote name="4376" id="4376" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--p">
            A 
            <strong class="markup--strong markup--blockquote-strong">template engine</strong> enables you to use static template files in your application. At runtime, the template engine replaces variables in a template file with actual values, and transforms the template into an HTML file sent to the client. This approach makes it easier to design an HTML page.
           </blockquote>
           <p name="1122" id="1122" class="graf graf--p graf-after--blockquote">The short version is that EJS allows us to interact with variables and then dynamically create our HTML based on those variables! (This will make a lot more sense later in the tutorial)</p>
           <p name="baac" id="baac" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">First, we’ll install ejs in the terminal:</p>
           <pre name="7738" id="7738" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">npm install ejs --save</pre>
           <p name="bac1" id="bac1" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">We can then set up our template engine with this line of code (just below our require statements) in our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">server.js</code> file:</p>
           <pre name="fffe" id="fffe" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">app.set('view engine', 'ejs')</pre>
           <p name="8ac1" id="8ac1" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre graf--trailing">EJS is accessed by default in the <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">views</code> directory. So create a new folder named <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">views</code> in your directory. Within that <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">views</code> folder, add a file named <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">index.ejs</code>. Think of our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">index.ejs</code> file as an HTML file for now.</p>
          </div>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section name="074c" class="section section--body">
         <div class="section-divider">
          <hr class="section-divider">
         </div>
         <div class="section-content">
          <div class="section-inner sectionLayout--insetColumn">
           <p name="8dfc" id="8dfc" class="graf graf--p graf--leading">Real quick, here’s what our file structure should look like thus far:</p>
           <pre name="99f6" id="99f6" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p graf--trailing">|-- weather-app<br>   |-- views<br>      |-- index.ejs<br>   |-- package.json<br>   |-- server.js</pre>
          </div>
         </div>
        </section>
        <section name="37db" class="section section--body">
         <div class="section-divider">
          <hr class="section-divider">
         </div>
         <div class="section-content">
          <div class="section-inner sectionLayout--insetColumn">
           <p name="e06e" id="e06e" class="graf graf--p graf--leading">Awesome, here’s a boilerplate for our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">index.ejs</code> file. I’m not going to go over this file as this is not an HTML tutorial, but it should be pretty straight forward as we’re not using any EJS just yet. The html is just a form with one input for a city, and one submit button:</p>
           <figure name="6b7e" id="6b7e" class="graf graf--figure graf--iframe graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 35.699999999999996%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia">
              <img src="https://i.embed.ly/1/display/resize?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07&amp;width=40" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <div class="iframeContainer">
               <iframe width="700" height="250" data-src="/media/0f78d29d82cbad974d272e83ae3fe8c9?postId=a317f904897b" data-media-id="0f78d29d82cbad974d272e83ae3fe8c9" data-thumbnail="https://i.embed.ly/1/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07" class="progressiveMedia-iframe js-progressiveMedia-iframe" allowfullscreen frameborder="0"></iframe>

              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <div class="iframeContainer">
                <iframe width="700" height="250" src="/media/0f78d29d82cbad974d272e83ae3fe8c9?postId=a317f904897b" data-media-id="0f78d29d82cbad974d272e83ae3fe8c9" data-thumbnail="https://i.embed.ly/1/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07" allowfullscreen frameborder="0"></iframe>
               </div>
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="9f2c" id="9f2c" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Once you have the above code copied into your <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">index.ejs</code> file, you’re almost done! The final thing we need to do is replace our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">app.get</code> code:</p>
           <pre name="6858" id="6858" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--pre-code u-paddingRight0 u-marginRight0">app.get('/', function (req, res) {<br><strong class="markup--strong markup--pre-strong"> // OLD CODE<br> res.send('Hello World!')</strong><br>})</code></pre>
           <p name="a444" id="a444" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Above is the old code where we send the text ‘Hello World!’ to the client. Instead, we want to send our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">index.ejs</code> file:</p>
           <pre name="b3f6" id="b3f6" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">app.get('/', function (req, res) {<br><strong class="markup--strong markup--pre-strong">  // NEW CODE<br>  res.render('index');</strong><br>})</pre>
           <p name="a216" id="a216" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Instead of using <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">res.send</code>, we use <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">res.render</code> when working with a templating language. <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">res.render</code> will render our view, then send the equivalent HTML to the client.</p>
           <p name="e84a" id="e84a" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">At this point, wee can test again by running:</p>
           <pre name="6d8e" id="6d8e" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--pre-strong">node server.js</strong></pre>
           <pre name="765e" id="765e" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// <code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">Example app listening on port 3000!</code></pre>
           <p name="8fc7" id="8fc7" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Now open your browser and visit: <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">localhost:3000</code> and you should see our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">index.ejs</code> file being displayed!</p>
           <figure name="6a19" id="6a19" class="graf graf--figure graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked" style="max-width: 613px; max-height: 181px;">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 29.5%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia graf-image" data-image-id="1*5sHe9cHrvfBLDa5HGFXY8Q.png" data-width="613" data-height="181">
              <img src="https://cdn-images-1.medium.com/freeze/max/60/1*5sHe9cHrvfBLDa5HGFXY8Q.png?q=20" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>

             What you should see at this&nbsp;point

           <h3 name="6bf5" id="6bf5" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--figure">Adding a CSS&nbsp;File</h3>
           <p name="6699" id="6699" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Yours will look a little less ‘pretty’ than mine. That’s because I’m making use of a css file to style my HTML. Here’s how we get our CSS to work:</p>
           <p name="500d" id="500d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">You’ll need to add a new folder to our project called <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">public</code>. Within that folder create a <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">css</code> folder, and finally create a file named <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">index.css</code>. Here’s your new file structure:</p>
           <pre name="9860" id="9860" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">|-- weather-app<br>   |-- views<br>      |-- index.ejs<br>   |-- public<br>      |-- css<br>         |-- index.js<br>   |-- package.json<br>   |-- server.js</pre>
           <p name="1884" id="1884" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Express wont allow access to this file by default, so we need to expose it with the following line of code:</p>
           <pre name="12c3" id="12c3" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">app.use(express.static('public'));</pre>
           <p name="16be" id="16be" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">This code allows us to access all of the static files within the ‘public’ folder.</p>
           <p name="ad44" id="ad44" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Finally, we need our CSS. Since this isn’t a CSS course, I’m not going to be going over the specifics, but if you’d like to use my CSS, you can copy it from <a href="https://github.com/bmorelli25/simple-nodejs-weather-app/blob/master/public/css/style.css" data-href="https://github.com/bmorelli25/simple-nodejs-weather-app/blob/master/public/css/style.css" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">here</a>.</p>
           <h3 name="0445" id="0445" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">Setting up our POST&nbsp;Route</h3>
           <p name="3389" id="3389" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">By now, your <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">server.js</code> file should look like this:</p>
           <figure name="8ec0" id="8ec0" class="graf graf--figure graf--iframe graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 35.699999999999996%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia">
              <img src="https://i.embed.ly/1/display/resize?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07&amp;width=40" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <div class="iframeContainer">
               <iframe width="700" height="250" data-src="/media/669518f91aea7acc18a2ab5398e09884?postId=a317f904897b" data-media-id="669518f91aea7acc18a2ab5398e09884" data-thumbnail="https://i.embed.ly/1/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07" class="progressiveMedia-iframe js-progressiveMedia-iframe" allowfullscreen frameborder="0"></iframe>
              </div>
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <div class="iframeContainer">
                <iframe width="700" height="250" src="/media/669518f91aea7acc18a2ab5398e09884?postId=a317f904897b" data-media-id="669518f91aea7acc18a2ab5398e09884" data-thumbnail="https://i.embed.ly/1/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07" allowfullscreen frameborder="0"></iframe>
               </div>
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <p name="3419" id="3419" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">We have one get route, and then we create our server. However, for our application to work, we need a post route as well. If you look at our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">index.ejs</code> file, you can see that our form is submitting a post request to the <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">/</code> route:</p>
           <pre name="e65f" id="e65f" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">&lt;form action="/" method="post"&gt;</pre>
           <p name="5b2d" id="5b2d" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Now that we know where our form is posting, we can set up the route! A post request looks just like a get request, with one minor change:</p>
           <pre name="9c72" id="9c72" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">app.<strong class="markup--strong markup--pre-strong">post</strong>('/', function (req, res) {<br>  res.render('index');<br>})</pre>
           <p name="5ce4" id="5ce4" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">But instead of just responding with the same html template, lets access the name of the city the user typed in as well. For this we need to use an <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Express Middleware</em>.</p>
           <p name="5ef3" id="5ef3" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Express is a minimalist framework. However, we can make use of <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">Middleware </em>(functions that have access to the <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">req</code> and <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">res</code> bodies) in order to preform more advanced tasks.</p>
           <p name="9a1c" id="9a1c" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">We’re going to make use of the <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">body-parser</code> middleware. <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">body-parser</code> allows us to make use of the key-value pairs stored on the <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">req-body</code> object. In this case, we’ll be able to access the city name the user typed in on the client side.</p>
           <p name="c68f" id="c68f" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">To use <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">body-parser</code>, we must install it first:</p>
           <pre name="df72" id="df72" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">npm install body-parser --save</pre>
           <p name="208a" id="208a" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Once installed, we can require it, and then make use of our middleware with the following line of code in our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">server.js</code></p>
           <pre name="051e" id="051e" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">const bodyParser = require('body-parser');<br>// ...<br>// ...</pre>
           <pre name="d4bd" id="d4bd" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">app.use(bodyParser.urlencoded({ extended: true }));</pre>
           <p name="b301" id="b301" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">For the scope of this project, it’s not necessary you understand exactly <em class="markup--em markup--p-em">how </em>that line of code works. Just know that by using <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">body-parser</code> we can make use of the <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">req.body</code> object.</p>
           <p name="d565" id="d565" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">Finally, we can now update our post request to log the value of ‘city’ to the console.</p>
           <pre name="da92" id="da92" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">app.<strong class="markup--strong markup--pre-strong">post</strong>('/', function (req, res) {<br>  res.render('index');<br>  console.log(req.body.city);<br>})</pre>
           <p name="5297" id="5297" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Lets test it!</p>
           <pre name="41d4" id="41d4" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p"><strong class="markup--strong markup--pre-strong">node server.js</strong></pre>
           <pre name="cb7d" id="cb7d" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// <code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">Example app listening on port 3000!</code></pre>
           <p name="ceb6" id="ceb6" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Now open your browser and visit: <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">localhost:3000</code>, type a city name into the field and hit enter!</p>
           <p name="769b" id="769b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">If you go back to your command prompt, you should see the city name displayed in the prompt! Awesome, you’ve now successfully passed data from the client to the server!</p>
           <p name="f714" id="f714" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">If you can’t get it to work, here’s what your <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">server.js</code> file should look like now:</p>
           <figure name="db7f" id="db7f" class="graf graf--figure graf--iframe graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 35.699999999999996%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia">
              <img src="https://i.embed.ly/1/display/resize?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07&amp;width=40" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <div class="iframeContainer">
               <iframe width="700" height="250" data-src="/media/49ff821fc14ffe7c483b755dad349139?postId=a317f904897b" data-media-id="49ff821fc14ffe7c483b755dad349139" data-thumbnail="https://i.embed.ly/1/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07" class="progressiveMedia-iframe js-progressiveMedia-iframe" allowfullscreen frameborder="0"></iframe>

              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <div class="iframeContainer">

           <h3 name="93b4" id="93b4" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--figure">Finishing app.post</h3>
           <p name="8233" id="8233" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">To finish up this project, you’ll need the code from my previous tutorial: <a href="https://codeburst.io/build-a-simple-weather-app-with-node-js-in-just-16-lines-of-code-32261690901d" data-href="https://codeburst.io/build-a-simple-weather-app-with-node-js-in-just-16-lines-of-code-32261690901d" class="markup--anchor markup--p-anchor" target="_blank">Build a simple Weather App with Node.js in just 16 lines of code</a>. I’ve copied in the code below. If you don’t understand what the code is doing, I recommend you go read through my previous tutorial.</p>
           <p name="5c7c" id="5c7c" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">What were going to do is make a request to the OpenWeatherMap API in our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">app.post</code> request. Here’s what the code looks like:</p>
           <figure name="a35d" id="a35d" class="graf graf--figure graf--iframe graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 35.699999999999996%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia">
              <img src="https://i.embed.ly/1/display/resize?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07&amp;width=40" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <div class="iframeContainer">
               <iframe width="700" height="250" data-src="/media/512255ccc51bcb89af163b47a725501b?postId=a317f904897b" data-media-id="512255ccc51bcb89af163b47a725501b" data-thumbnail="https://i.embed.ly/1/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07" class="progressiveMedia-iframe js-progressiveMedia-iframe" allowfullscreen frameborder="0"></iframe>
              </div>
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <div class="iframeContainer">
                <iframe width="700" height="250" src="/media/512255ccc51bcb89af163b47a725501b?postId=a317f904897b" data-media-id="512255ccc51bcb89af163b47a725501b" data-thumbnail="https://i.embed.ly/1/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07" allowfullscreen frameborder="0"></iframe>
               </div>
              </noscript>
             </div>

           </figure>
           <p name="63e8" id="63e8" class="graf graf--p graf-after--figure">Woah. That’s a lot of new code. Lets break it all down:</p>
           <h4 name="876b" id="876b" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--p">1. Setting up our&nbsp;URL:</h4>
           <p name="0d72" id="0d72" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">The first thing we do when we receive the post request is grab the <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">city</code> off of <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">req.body</code>. Then we create a <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">url</code> string that we’ll use to access the OpenWeatherMap API with</p>
           <pre name="e276" id="e276" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">app.post('/', function (req, res) {<br>  let city = req.body.city;<br>  let url = `<a href="http://api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5/weather?q=$%7Bcity%7D&amp;units=imperial&amp;appid=$%7BapiKey%7D`" data-href="http://api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5/weather?q=${city}&amp;units=imperial&amp;appid=${apiKey}`" class="markup--anchor markup--pre-anchor" rel="nofollow noopener noopener" target="_blank">http://api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5/weather?q=${city}&amp;units=imperial&amp;appid=${apiKey}`</a></pre>
           <h4 name="a34d" id="a34d" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--pre">2. Make our API&nbsp;call:</h4>
           <p name="a4a7" id="a4a7" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Now that we have our URL, we can make our API call. When we receive our callback, the first thing we’re going to do is check for an error. If we have an error, we’re going to render our index page. But notice that I’ve also added in a second argument. <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">res.render</code> has an optional second argument?—?an object where we can specify properties to be handled by our view ( <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">index.ejs</code> ).</p>
           <p name="22bd" id="22bd" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">In this instance, I’ve added an error string:</p>
           <pre name="82e1" id="82e1" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">request(url, function (err, response, body) {<br>    if(err){<br>      res.render('index', {weather: null, error: 'Error, please try again'});</pre>
           <h4 name="fa90" id="fa90" class="graf graf--h4 graf-after--pre">3. Display the&nbsp;weather:</h4>
           <p name="6aa4" id="6aa4" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h4">Now that we know we have no API error, we can parse our JSON into a usable JavaScript object.</p>
           <p name="53dc" id="53dc" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">The first thing we’ll do is check to see if <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">weather.main == undefined</code>&nbsp;. The only reason why this would be undefined, is if our user input a string that isn’t a city (‘3’, ‘afefaefefe’, etc.). In this instance, we’ll render the index view, and we’ll also pass back an error.</p>
           <p name="ae82" id="ae82" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">If <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">weather.main&nbsp;!= undefined</code>, then we can finally send back the weather to the client! We’ll create a string that clarifies what the weather is, and send that back with the index view.</p>
           <pre name="4d43" id="4d43" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">} else {<br>  let weather = JSON.parse(body)</pre>
           <pre name="96c7" id="96c7" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">  if(weather.main == undefined){<br>    res.render('index', {weather: null, error: 'Error, please try again'});<br>  } else {<br>    let weatherText = `It's ${weather.main.temp} degrees in ${weather.name}!`;<br>    res.render('index', {weather: weatherText, error: null});<br>  }<br>}</pre>
           <h3 name="d8e6" id="d8e6" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--pre">Using EJS</h3>
           <p name="341b" id="341b" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">There’s only one thing left to do at this point… Make use of all those variables we sent back with our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">res.render</code> call. These variables aren’t available on the client, this is where we finally get to use EJS. There are three possible scenarios that we have in our code:</p>
           <ol class="postList">
            <li name="4a81" id="4a81" class="graf graf--li graf-after--p"><code class="markup--code markup--li-code">{weather: null, error: null}</code></li>
            <li name="e009" id="e009" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li"><code class="markup--code markup--li-code">{weather: null, error: ‘Error, please try again’}</code></li>
            <li name="813b" id="813b" class="graf graf--li graf-after--li"><code class="markup--code markup--li-code">{weather: weatherText, error: null}</code></li>
           </ol>
           <p name="72dc" id="72dc" class="graf graf--p graf-after--li">We need to make two simple changes to our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">index.ejs</code> to handle these three scenarios. Here’s the code, then I’ll walk you through it:</p>
           <pre name="ec1a" id="ec1a" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--p">&lt;% if(weather !== null){ %&gt;<br>  &lt;p&gt;&lt;%= weather %&gt;&lt;/p&gt;<br>&lt;% } %&gt;</pre>
           <pre name="3476" id="3476" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">&lt;% if(error !== null){ %&gt;<br>  &lt;p&gt;&lt;%= error %&gt;&lt;/p&gt;<br>&lt;% } %&gt;</pre>
           <p name="f1b8" id="f1b8" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">It helps to remember that EJS stands for Embedded JavaScript. With that in mind, EJS has opening and closing brackets: <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">&lt;% CODE HERE %&gt;</code> Anything between the brackets is executed. If the opening bracket also includes an equal sign: <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">&lt;%= CODE HERE ADDS HTML %&gt;</code>, then that code will add HTML to the result.</p>
           <p name="8acc" id="8acc" class="graf graf--p graf-after--p">If you look at our EJS that we’ve added, we’re testing to see if either of our <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">weather</code>, or <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">error</code> variables are null. If they’re both <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">null</code>, nothing happens. However, if one isn’t null (i.e. it has a value), then we will add a paragraph to the screen with the value of the respective variable.</p>
           <h3 name="500c" id="500c" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--p">index.ejs</h3>
           <p name="3b1c" id="3b1c" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Here’s what your <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">index.ejs</code> should look like:</p>
           <figure name="8898" id="8898" class="graf graf--figure graf--iframe graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 35.699999999999996%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia">
              <img src="https://i.embed.ly/1/display/resize?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07&amp;width=40" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <div class="iframeContainer">
               <iframe width="700" height="250" data-src="/media/17432e735bdb5fb7416e63e8235f7af0?postId=a317f904897b" data-media-id="17432e735bdb5fb7416e63e8235f7af0" data-thumbnail="https://i.embed.ly/1/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07" class="progressiveMedia-iframe js-progressiveMedia-iframe" allowfullscreen frameborder="0"></iframe>
              </div>
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <div class="iframeContainer">
                <iframe width="700" height="250" src="/media/17432e735bdb5fb7416e63e8235f7af0?postId=a317f904897b" data-media-id="17432e735bdb5fb7416e63e8235f7af0" data-thumbnail="https://i.embed.ly/1/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07" allowfullscreen frameborder="0"></iframe>
               </div>
              </noscript>
             </div>
            </div>
           </figure>
           <h3 name="9878" id="9878" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--figure">server.js</h3>
           <p name="0d24" id="0d24" class="graf graf--p graf-after--h3">Here’s what your <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">server.js</code> should look like:</p>
           <figure name="f488" id="f488" class="graf graf--figure graf--iframe graf-after--p">
            <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder is-locked">
             <div class="aspectRatioPlaceholder-fill" style="padding-bottom: 35.699999999999996%;"></div>
             <div class="progressiveMedia js-progressiveMedia">
              <img src="https://i.embed.ly/1/display/resize?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07&amp;width=40" crossorigin="anonymous" class="progressiveMedia-thumbnail js-progressiveMedia-thumbnail">
              <canvas class="progressiveMedia-canvas js-progressiveMedia-canvas"></canvas>
              <div class="iframeContainer">
               <iframe width="700" height="250" data-src="/media/3bd8d68977725c4ae3200553369b24e2?postId=a317f904897b" data-media-id="3bd8d68977725c4ae3200553369b24e2" data-thumbnail="https://i.embed.ly/1/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07" class="progressiveMedia-iframe js-progressiveMedia-iframe" allowfullscreen frameborder="0"></iframe>
              </div>
              <noscript class="js-progressiveMedia-inner">
               <div class="iframeContainer">
                <iframe width="700" height="250" src="/media/3bd8d68977725c4ae3200553369b24e2?postId=a317f904897b" data-media-id="3bd8d68977725c4ae3200553369b24e2" data-thumbnail="https://i.embed.ly/1/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Favatars3.githubusercontent.com%2Fu%2F5618806%3Fv%3D3%26s%3D400&amp;key=a19fcc184b9711e1b4764040d3dc5c07" allowfullscreen frameborder="0"></iframe>
               </div>

           <h3 name="27a7" id="27a7" class="graf graf--h3 graf-after--figure">Run your&nbsp;code</h3>
           <blockquote name="0766" id="0766" class="graf graf--blockquote graf-after--h3">
            Reminder: all of the code for this project can be found in the 
            <a href="https://github.com/bmorelli25/simple-nodejs-weather-app" data-href="https://github.com/bmorelli25/simple-nodejs-weather-app" class="markup--anchor markup--blockquote-anchor" rel="noopener" target="_blank">GitHub Repo</a>
           </blockquote>
           <pre name="c4d8" id="c4d8" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--blockquote"><strong class="markup--strong markup--pre-strong">node server.js</strong></pre>
           <pre name="c639" id="c639" class="graf graf--pre graf-after--pre">// <code class="markup--code markup--pre-code">Example app listening on port 3000!</code></pre>
           <p name="ffa5" id="ffa5" class="graf graf--p graf-after--pre">Now open your browser and visit: <code class="markup--code markup--p-code">localhost:3000</code>, type a city name into the field and hit enter! You should see the weather appear on your screen!</p>
